There shall be credited to the capital account-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        such proportion of grants by Government under clause (b) of sub-section (2) of section 44, as may be fixed by the Government from time to time;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        loans obtained from Government;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        loans obtained by the Authority with special or general sanction of the Government;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        foreign aid and loans obtained from the Development Loan Fund;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        the proceeds of the sale of any land vested in the Authority which was purchased out of any loan;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         the proceeds of the sale of any movable property (including securities for money invested from the capital account) belonging to the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        any other sum which the Government may direct to be credited to the capital account.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Application of capital account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">59. The moneys credited to the capital account shall be held by the Authority in trust, and shall be applied to-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        meeting all costs of framing and executing improvement, development and re-housing schemes;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        meeting the cost of acquiring land for carrying out any of the purposes of this Ordinance;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        meeting the cost of constructing buildings required for carrying out any of the purposes of this Ordinance;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        the repayment of loans from money borrowed in pursuance of clauses (c), (d) and (e) of sub-section (2) of section 44;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        making, or contributing towards the cost of making, surveys in pursuance of section 42;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         meeting such proportion of the cost of management as the Authority may, with the sanction of the Government, fix in this behalf; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        temporarily making good the deficit (if any) in the revenue account at the end of any financial year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Credit to revenue account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">60. There shall be credited to the revenue account-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) contribution of the Corporation under section 45;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) such proportion of grants made by Government under clause (b) of sub-section (2) of section 44, as may be fixed by the Government from time to time;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) proceeds of any improvement or betterment levy, water rate, conservancy rate or any other rate levied by the Authority with the sanction of Government under clause (f) of sub-section (2) of section 44;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) all interest received by the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) all damages received by the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         all annually recurring sums received from the Government in aid of the funds of the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) all premia received by the Authority in connection with leases;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h) all rents of land and buildings vested in the Authority; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         any other sums which the Government may direct to be credited to the revenue account.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Application of revenue account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">61. The moneys credited to the revenue account shall be held by the Authority in trust, and shall be applied to-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) meeting all charges for interest due on account of any loan taken in pursuance of clauses (c), (d) or (e) of sub-section (2) of section 44 and all other charges incurred in connection with such loans;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) paying all sums due from the Authority in respect of rates and taxes imposed under the 34[ Chittagong City Corporation Ordinance, 1982 (Ord. No. XXXV of 1982)], upon land vested in the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) paying the cost (if any) of maintaining a separate Establishment for the collection of the rents and other proceeds of land vested in the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) paying all sums which the Government may direct to be paid to an auditor under section 69;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        making payments in pursuance of section 94 for compensation or for expenses of maintenance of works; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) paying the cost of management.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- The expression “cost of management” means-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the salary and allowances of the Chairman and fees of the Members of the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) all fees and allowances paid for attendance at meeting;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        the salaries, fees and allowances of, and the contributions paid under the proviso to section 18 in respect of employees of the Authority appointed under that section; except employees who are paid by the day or whose pay is charged to temporary work; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        all office expenses incurred by the Authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- “Office expenses” means expenses incurred for carrying on office work, and includes the rent of offices, the provision of furniture therefore, the charges for printing and stationery and any other incidental expenses necessary for the efficient working of an office.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Advances from revenue account to capital account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">62. (1) Notwithstanding anything contained in section 61, the Authority may advance any sum standing at the credit of the revenue account for the purpose of meeting capital expenditure.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every such advance shall be refunded to the revenue account as soon as may be practicable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Advances from capital account to revenue account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">63. (1) Any deficit in the revenue account at the end of any financial year may be made good by an advance from the capital account.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every such advance shall be refunded to the capital account in the following financial year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Submission of abstract of accounts</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">64. (1) The Authority shall submit to the Government at the end of each half of every financial year, an abstract of the accounts of their receipts and expenditures.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Submission of yearly reports and returns</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">65. (1) The Authority shall submit to the Government, as soon as possible but within three months after the end of every financial year, a report on the conduct of its affairs for that year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may require the Authority to furnish-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) any return, statement, estimate, statistics or other information regarding any matter under the control of the Authority, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) a report on any such matter, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) a copy of any document in the charge of the Authority;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">and the Authority shall comply with every such requisition.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Recovery of dues of Authority</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">66. The Authority shall have power to realise its dues from any person under the 35[ * * *] Public Demands Recovery Act, 1913, as a public demand.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Annual audit of accounts</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">67. The accounts of the Authority shall, once in every financial year, be examined and audited by such Auditor as the Government may appoint in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of Auditors</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">68. The Auditor so appointed may,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) by written summons, require the production before him of any document which he may consider necessary for the proper conduct of the audit;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        by written summons, require any person having the custody or control of, or being accountable for, any such document to appear in person before him; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) require any person so appearing before him to make and sign a declaration with respect to any such document to answer any questions, or to prepare and submit any statement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Remuneration of Auditor</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">69. The Authority shall pay to the said Auditor such remuneration as the Government may direct.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Auditor’s report</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">70. The Auditor shall-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        report to the Authority any material impropriety or irregularity which he may observe in the expenditure,                      </p></div></div>
264	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">   THE CHITTAGONG MUSLIM INSTITUTE ORDINANCE, 1959 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CHITTAGONG MUSLIM INSTITUTE ORDINANCE, 1959</strong></p><p align="center">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. LXV OF 1959)</p><p align="right">[24th September, 1959]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS by an Indenture of Exchange dated the 13th day of December, 1946, executed by the Chittagong Muslim Institute Committee and the Governor of Bengal, the properties described in the Schedule to this Ordinance were conveyed to the said Chittagong Muslim Institute Committee; 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS the said Chittagong Muslim Institute Committee has since then been in possession of the aforesaid properties along with all buildings, erections, fixtures, fittings and movables;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS the said Chittagong Muslim Institute Committee has, by a resolution dated the 7th day of December, 1958, agreed to the taking over of the possession, control and management of the lands described in the Schedule to this Ordinance together with all buildings, erections, fittings, fixtures and movables by the Government;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is expedient to make provision for taking over possession, control and management of the properties described in the Schedule to this Ordinance for the purpose of establishment of a public library, free reading room and Assembly Hall;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Presidential Proclamation of the seventh day of October, 1958, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor of East Pakistan is pleased to make and promulgate following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the Chittagong Muslim Institute Ordinance, 1959.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Transfer to and vesting in the Government of the Chittagong Muslim Institute</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. As from the date of promulgation of this Ordinance, the institution heretofore known as the Chittagong Muslim Institute and the Musafirkhana with attached Mosque together with the lands described in the Schedule to this Ordinance and all buildings and other erections standing or being thereon with all fixtures and fittings and all movable properties, funds, moneys, rights and powers which, immediately before the commencement of this Ordinance, were vested in, or held by, the Chittagong Muslim Institute Committee, shall be transferred to, and shall be vested in and held by, the Government free from all encumbrances and without payment of any compensation whatsoever.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Protection of action taken under this Ordinance</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. No suit, prosecution or other legal proceedings shall lie against the Government or any person for anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done in pursuance of this Ordinance or any order made thereunder.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) The Government may make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may provide for management, control and preservation of the Chittagong Muslim Institute, the Musafirkhana and the Mosque attached to it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_________________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
265	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CIVIL AVIATION ORDINANCE, 1960 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CIVIL AVIATION ORDINANCE, 1960</strong></p><p align="center">(ORDINANCE NO. XXXII OF 1960)</p><p align="right">[27th July, 1960]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Ordinance to make better provision for the control of manufacture, possession, use, operation, sale, import and export of aircraft, the control and regulation of air transport services, and the control and development of aerodromes in Bangladesh.            1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to make better provision for the control of manufacture, possession, use, operation, sale, import and export of aircraft, the control and regulation of air transport services, and the control and development of aerodromes in Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Proclamation of the seventh day of October, 1958, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the President is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and application </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the Civil Aviation Ordinance, 1960.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh, and applies to all citizens of Bangladesh and persons on any aircraft registered in Bangladesh, wherever such citizens or persons may be, and to all persons on any aircraft while in Bangladesh, but nothing in this Ordinance or the rules or in any order made thereunder-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        shall apply to or in respect of any aircraft belonging to or exclusively employed in the naval, military or air force of Bangladesh, or persons employed in connection with any such aircraft, unless the Government, by notification in the official Gazette, applies to any such aircraft or person, with or without modification, any of the provisions of this Ordinance or the rules; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        shall apply to or in respect of any lighthouse to which the Lighthouse Act, 1927, applies, or prejudice or affect any right or power exercisable by any authority under that Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Ordinance, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) “aerodrome” means any area of land or water designed, equipped, set apart or commonly used or intended to be used, either wholly or in part, for affording facilities for the landing and departure of aircraft, and includes all buildings, sheds, vessels, piers, and other structures thereon or appertaining thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) “aircraft” means any machine which can derive support in the atmosphere from reactions of the air, and includes balloons, whether captive or free, airships, kites, gliders and flying machines;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) “airport” means an aerodrome at which facilities have, in the opinion of the Government, been sufficiently developed to be of importance to civil aviation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) “air transport service” means a service of aircraft for the purpose of effecting public transport of passengers, goods, mails and other things;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) “commercial flying” means flying for carriage by air of any passenger, mail or goods for hire or reward and such other flying for the purposes of any trade or business as may be specified by the Government and “commercial flight” shall be construed accordingly;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) “export” means taking out of Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) “import” means bringing into Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        “landing area” means the part of the movement area intended for the landing or take off run of aircraft;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         “prescribed” means prescribed by rules;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j)         “purposes of civil aviation” include all purposes connected with air navigation except purposes of defence by air;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k)        “rules” means the rules made under this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to exempt, etc</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, either exempt from all or any of the provisions of this Ordinance 2[ or the rules] any aircraft or class of aircraft, and any person or class of persons, or may direct that all or any of such provisions shall apply to any aircraft or person subject to such modifications or conditions as may be specified in the notification.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules to implement certain International Conventions</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make such rules as appear to it to be necessary for carrying out the provisions of-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        the Convention on International Civil Aviation signed in Chicago on the seventh day of December, 1944, and any amendments of the Convention or annex thereto made in accordance with the provisions of Article 94 of the Convention;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3[ (aa) the Convention on International Recognition of Rights in Aircraft signed in Geneva on the nineteenth day of June, 1948, and any amendment thereto;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(aaa) the Convention on Damage caused by Foreign Aircraft to Third Parties on the Surface signed in Rome on the seventh day of October, 1952, and any amendment thereto;]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4[ * * *] and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        any other treaty, agreement or convention between Bangladesh and any other country or any decision taken at any international body relating to civil aviation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules generally</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may provide for one or more of the following matters, that is to say-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the authorities by which any of the powers conferred by or under this Ordinance are to be exercised;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the regulation of air transport services and commercial flying, and the prohibition of the use of aircraft in such services and in commercial flights except under the authority of, and in accordance with, a licence authorising the establishment of any such service or flight;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the information to be furnished by an applicant for, or the holder of, a licence authorising the establishment of an air transport service to such authorities as may be prescribed;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        the licensing, inspection and regulation of aerodromes or airports, the conditions under which aerodromes or airports may be maintained, and the fees which may be charged for the use of, and for services provided at, such aerodromes or airports, and the prohibition or regulation of the use of unlicensed aerodromes or air ports, and the regulation of conduct of persons at aerodromes or airports or in the vicinity of aerodromes or airports;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        the inspection and control of the manufacture, repair and maintenance of aircraft and of places where air craft are manufactured, repaired or kept;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) the registration and marking of aircraft;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5[ (ff) the hire, charter, lease, hypothecation or mortgage of aircraft;]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        the conditions under which aircraft may be flown, or may carry passengers, goods, mails and other things, or may be used for industrial purposes, and the certificates, licences or documents to be carried by aircraft;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        the inspection or supervision of aircraft for the purpose of enforcing the provisions of this Ordinance and the rules, and the facilities to be provided for such inspection or supervision;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         the conditions subject to which persons may be engaged or employed in, or in connection with, air navigation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j)         the licensing of persons employed in the operation, manufacture, repair or maintenance of aircraft and at aerodromes or airports;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k)        the conditions under which, and the aerodromes or airports to or from which, aircraft entering or leaving Bangladesh may fly, and the conditions under which aircraft may fly over Bangladesh or from one place in Bangladesh to another;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(l)         the prohibition of flight by aircraft over any specified area, either absolutely or at specified times, or subject to specified conditions and exceptions;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(m)       the supply, supervision and control of air-route beacons, aerodrome or airport lights, and lights at or in the neighbourhood of aerodromes or airports and on or in the neighbourhood of air-routes;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(n)        the formulation and observance of uniform standards in respect of obstruction clearances for areas adjoining the landing area at aerodromes and airports;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(o)        the installation and maintenance of lights on private property in the neighbourhood of aerodromes or airports and on or in the neighbourhood of air-routes, by the owners or occupiers of such property, payment by the Government for such installation and maintenance, and supervision and control of such installation and maintenance, including the right of access to the property for such purpose, and the removal of lights, radio and electrical equipment and smoke producing apparatus which may endanger the safety of aircraft in the vicinity of aerodromes or airports;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(p)        the regulation and making of signals and communications by or to aircraft, and by or to persons carried therein;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(q)        the measures to be taken for securing the requirements of obstruction clearance at aerodromes and airports, for the safety, efficiency and regularity of air navigation and the safety of aircraft, passengers, goods, mails and other things carried therein, and for preventing aircraft from endangering other persons and property;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(r)        the prohibition or regulation of carriage in aircraft of any specified article or substance;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(s)        the issue and maintenance of log-books;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(t) the manner in which and the conditions subject to which any licence or certificate may be issued under this Ordinance or the rules, the examination and tests to be undergone in connection therewith, and the form, custody, production, endorsement, cancellation, suspension or surrender of any such licence or certificate, or of any log-book;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(u)        the fees to be charged in connection with any inspection, examination, test, certificate or licence, made, issued, or renewed under this Ordinance or the rules;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(v) the recognition, for the purposes of this Ordinance, of licences and certificates issued elsewhere than in Bangladesh relating to aircraft or to the qualifications of persons employed in the operation, manufacture, repair or maintenance of aircraft;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(w) the supply, for purposes of air navigation, of meteorological information by persons engaged or employed in connection with air navigation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(x) the regulation of the use of the civil air ensign and any other ensign established by the Government in connection with air navigation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(y)        any matter subsidiary or incidental to matters referred to in this sub-section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make orders in times of war or emergency</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) In the event of war or other emergency, or in the interests of public safety or tranquility, if the Government is of opinion that the issue of all or any of the following orders is expedient, it may, by notification in the official Gazette,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        cancel or suspend, either absolutely or subject to such conditions as it may think fit to specify in the order, all or any of the licences or certificates issued under this Ordinance or the rules;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        prohibit, either absolutely or subject to such conditions as it may think fit to specify in the order, or regulate in such manner as may be specified in the order, the flight of all or any aircraft or class of aircraft over the whole or any part of Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        prohibit, either absolutely or conditionally, or regulate the construction, maintenance or use of any aerodrome or airport, aircraft factory, flying-school or club, or place where aircraft are manufactured, repaired or kept, or any class or description thereof; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        direct that any aircraft or class of aircraft or any aerodrome or airport, aircraft factory, flying-school or club, or place where aircraft are manufactured, repaired or kept, together with any machinery, plant, material or things used for the operation, manufacture, repair or maintenance of aircraft shall be delivered forthwith or within a specified time, for being placed at the disposal of the Government, to such authority and in such manner as it may specify in the order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Any person who suffers direct injury or loss by reason of any order made under clause (c) of sub-section (1) or by the delivery of any aircraft or class of aircraft in pursuance of clause (d) of that sub-section, shall be paid such compensation as may be determined by such authority as the Government may appoint in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Any person interested in any such aerodrome or airport, aircraft factory, flying-school or club, or place where aircraft are manufactured, repaired or kept as is delivered in pursuance of clause (d) of sub-section (1) shall be paid compensation the amount of which shall be determined in the manner and in accordance with the principles hereinafter set out, that is to say,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) where the amount of compensation can be fixed by agreement, it shall be paid in accordance with such agreement;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        where no such agreement can be reached, the Government shall appoint as arbitrator a person qualified for appointment as Judge of 6[ the Supreme Court];</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        the Government may, in any particular case, nominate a person having expert knowledge as to the nature of the property acquired, to assist the arbitrator, and where such nomination is made, the person to be compensated may also nominate an assessor for the said purpose;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) at the commencement of the proceedings before the arbitrator, the Government and the person to be compensated shall state what in their respective opinions is a fair amount of compensation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) the arbitrator in making his award shall have regard to-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         the provisions mutatis mutandis of 7[ section 9 of the Acquisition and Requisition of Immovable Property Ordinance, 1982]; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii) the permanent or temporary nature of the acquisition;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         an appeal shall lie to the 8[ High Court Division] against the award of an arbitrator except in cases where the amount thereof does not exceed the amount prescribed in this behalf;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        save as provided in this sub-section or the rules, nothing in any law for the time being in force shall apply to arbitrations under this sub-section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Government may authorise such steps to be taken to secure compliance with any order made under sub-section (1) as appear to it to be necessary.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) Whoever knowingly disobeys, fails to comply with, or does any act in contravention of an order made under sub-section (1) shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years, or with fine which may extend to five thousand taka, or with both, and the court by</p><p style="text-align: justify;">which he is convicted may direct that the aircraft or thing, if any, in respect of which the offence has been committed, or any part of such thing, shall be forfeited to the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules for investigation of accidents</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. (1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules providing for the investigation of any accident arising out of or in the course of the navigation-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        in or over Bangladesh, of any aircraft; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        anywhere, of aircraft registered in Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) require notice to be given of any accident in such manner and by such person as may be prescribed;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        apply for the purposes of such investigation, either with or without modification, the provisions of any law for the time being in force relating to the investigation of accidents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        prohibit, pending investigation, access to, or interference with, an aircraft to which an accident has occurred, and authorize any person, so far as may be necessary for the purposes of investigation, to have access to, examine, remove, take measures for the preservation of, or otherwise deal with, any such aircraft; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        authorise or require the cancellation, suspension, endorsement or surrender of any licence or certificate granted or recognized under this Ordinance or the rules, if it appears on investigation that the licence ought to be so dealt with, and provide for the production of any such licence for such purpose.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to detain aircraft</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. (1) Any authority authorised in this behalf by the Government may detain any aircraft, if in the opinion of such authority-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) having regard to the nature of an intended flight, the flight of such aircraft would involve danger to persons in the aircraft or to any other person or property; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        such detention is necessary to secure compliance with any of the provisions of this Ordinance or the rules or to prevent a contravention of any rule made under clause (i), (j) or (k) of sub-section (2) of section 5.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules regulating all matters incidental or subsidiary to the exercise of the powers conferred by sub-section (1).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules for protecting public health</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules for the prevention of danger arising to public health by the introduction or spread of any infectious or contagious disease from aircraft arriving or being at any aerodrome or airport and for the prevention of the conveyance of infection or contagion by means of any aircraft leaving an aerodrome or airport, and in particular and without prejudice to the generality of this provision may make, with respect to aircraft and aerodromes or airports or any specified aerodrome or airport, rules providing for any of the matters for which rules under sub- clauses (i) to (viii) of clause (p) of sub-section (1) of section 6 of the Ports Act, 1908, may be made with respect to vessels and ports.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Emergency powers for protecting public health</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. (1) If the Government is satisfied that Bangladesh or any part thereof is visited by, or threatened with, an outbreak of any dangerous epidemic disease, and that the ordinary provisions of the law for the time being in force are insufficient for the prevention of danger arising to public health through the introduction or spread of the disease by the agency of aircraft, the Government may take such measures as it deems necessary to prevent such danger.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In any such case the Government, without prejudice to the powers conferred by section 9, may, by notification in the official Gazette, make such provisional rules with respect to aircraft and persons travelling or goods, mails and other things carried therein, and aerodromes or airports, as it deems necessary in the circumstances.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Notwithstanding anything contained in section 15, the power to make rules under sub-section (2) shall not be subject to the condition of previous publication, but such rules shall not remain in force for more than three months from the date of notification:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that the Government may, by special order, continue them in force for a further period or periods of not more than three months in all.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Penalty for flying so as to cause danger</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. Where an aircraft is flown in such manner as may cause unnecessary danger to any person or property on land or water, the pilot or the person in charge of the aircraft, and, unless he proves to the satisfaction of the court that the aircraft was so flown without his actual fault or privity, the owner thereof, shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to 9[ one year, or with fine which may extend to five thousand taka], or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- In this section “owner” in relation to an aircraft includes any person by whom the aircraft is chartered at the time the offence is committed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Wreck and salvage</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. (1) The provisions of Part VII of the Merchant Shipping Act, 1923, relating to wreck and salvage shall apply to an aircraft in, on or over, the sea or in tidal waters, or on or over the shores of the sea or tidal waters as they apply to ships, and the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make such modifications of the said provisions in their application to aircraft as appear to it to be necessary or expedient.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Any services rendered in assisting or in saving life from, or in saving the cargo or apparel of an aircraft in, on or over, the sea or in tidal waters, or on or over the shores of the sea or any tidal water, shall be deemed to be salvage in cases in which they would have been salvaged had they been rendered in relation to a ship, and where services are rendered by an aircraft to any property or person, salvour shall be entitled to the same reward for those services as he would have been entitled to had the aircraft been a ship.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The provisions of sub-section (2) shall have effect not- withstanding that the aircraft concerned is a foreign aircraft and that the services in question are rendered elsewhere than within the limits of the territorial waters of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Use of patent</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. The provisions of section 42 of the Patents And Designs Act, 1911, shall apply to the use of an invention on any aircraft not registered in Bangladesh in like manner as they apply to the use of an invention in a foreign vessel.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">14. [Power to apply customs procedure.- Repealed by the Fourth Schedule of the Customs Act, 1969 (Act No. IV of 1969).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Provisions relating to rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">15. (1) Rules may provide that a breach of any of them shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term not exceeding 10[ one year or with fine not exceeding five thousand taka] or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Save as provided in sub-section (3) of section 10, any power to make rules conferred by this Ordinance is subject to the condition of previous publication, and a period of not less than three weeks shall have elapsed between such publication and the making of the rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Rules may provide that, notwithstanding anything contained in the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, or in any other law for the time being in force, any officer specified therein may try in a summary way in accordance with the provisions in sections 262 to 265 of the Code an offence of any breach of, or failure to comply with, any rule for the safety of aircraft, passengers, goods, mails or other things carried therein or for preventing aircraft from endangering other persons or property, or to compound any such offence for a sum not exceeding 11[ three thousand taka].</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) An officer trying an offence in accordance with the rules made under sub-section (3) shall, for the purpose of the trial, be deemed to be Magistrate of the first class under the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, and any sentence passed by such officer shall be deemed to be a sentence passed by such Magistrate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Penalty for abetment of offences and attempted offences</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">16. Whoever abets the commission of any offence under this Ordinance or the rules, or attempts to commit such offence and in such attempt does any act towards the commission of the offence, shall be liable to the punishment provided for the offence.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of court to order forfeiture</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">17. Where any person is convicted of an offence for breach of any rule made under clause (l) or clause (r) of sub-section (2) of section 5, the court by which he is convicted may direct that the aircraft or article or substance, as the case may be, in respect of which the offence has been committed, shall be forfeited to the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bar to certain suits</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">18. No suit shall be brought in any civil court in respect of trespass or in respect of nuisance by reason only of the flight of aircraft over any property at a height above the ground which having regard to wind, whether and all the circumstances of the case is reasonable, or by reason only of the ordinary incidents of such flight.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Protection of acts done in good faith</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">19. No suit, prosecution or other legal proceeding shall lie against any person for anything in good faith done or intended to be done under this Ordinance or the rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">20. [Repeal.- Repealed by section 2 and 1st Schedule of the Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1965 (Ordinance No. X of 1965).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">__________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the words “Bangladesh”, “Government” and “taka” were substituted for the words “Pakistan”, “Central Government” and “rupees” respectively by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “or the rules” were inserted by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 Clauses (aa) and (aaa) were inserted by section 2 of the Civil Aviation (Amendment) Act, 1988 (Act No. XLIV of 1988)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 Clauses (b) and (c) were omitted by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 Clause (ff) was inserted by section 3 of the Civil Aviation (Amendment) Act, 1988 (Act No. XLIV of 1988)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The words “the Supreme Court” were substituted for the words “a High Court” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The words, figures and comma “section 9 of the Acquisition and Requisition of Immovable Property Ordinance, 1982” were substituted for the words, brackets, figures and comma “sub-section (1) of section 23 of the Land Acquisition Act, 1894” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8 The words “High Court Division” were substituted for the words “High Court” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9 The words and comma “one year, or with fine which may extend to five thousand taka” were substituted for the words and comma “six months, or with fine which may extend to one thousand rupees” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10 The words “one year or with fine not exceeding five thousand taka” were substituted for the words “three months or with fine not exceeding one thousand rupees” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11 The words “three thousand taka” were substituted for the words “one thousand rupees” by section 2 of the Civil Aviation Laws Amendment Ordinance, 1985 (Ordinance No. XXIII of 1985)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
266	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">   THE CLAIMS FOR MAINTENANCE (RECOVERY ABROAD) ORDINANCE, 1959 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CLAIMS FOR MAINTENANCE (RECOVERY ABROAD) ORDINANCE, 1959</strong></p><p align="center">(ORDINANCE NO. L OF 1959)</p><p align="right">[10th September, 1959]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An  Ordinance to give effect to the United Nations Convention on the Recovery Abroad of Claims for Maintenance.      1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS the United Nations Conference on Maintenance Obligations held at New York from the 29th May, 1956, to the 20th June, 1956, adopted the Convention on the Recovery Abroad of Maintenance;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS Article 13 of the said Convention provides that the Convention may be acceded to at any time on behalf of any Member of the United Nations;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS Bangladesh, being a Member of the United Nations, has, in pursuance of the aforesaid Article, acceded to the Convention on the fourteenth day of July, 1959;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is expedient to give effect to the Convention;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Proclamation of the seventh day of October, 1958, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the President is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Short title and commencement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the Claims for Maintenance (Recovery Abroad) Ordinance, 1959.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Definitions</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Ordinance, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Article” means an article of the Convention;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “Contracting Party” means Bangladesh, and any other state whose instrument of ratification or accession is deposited under Article 13 and which is notified by the Government in the official Gazette to be a Contracting Party;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) “Convention” means the United Nations Convention on the Recovery Abroad of Maintenance; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) “Transmitting Agency” and “Receiving Agency” for a Contracting Party shall mean respectively the judicial or administrative authority and the public or private body designated under Article 2 to be the Transmitting Agency or the Receiving Agency, as the case may be, and notified as such by the Government in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Publication of information</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. The Government shall, from time to time, publish in the official Gazette any information received by it from the Secretary-General of the United Nations in pursuance of Article 19.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>The Convention to have the force of law in Bangladesh</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in any other law, the provisions of the Convention set out in the Schedule shall have the force of law in Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may amend the Schedule in conformity with such amendments as may, from time to time, be made in the Convention.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to make rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. The Government may make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_____________________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the words “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Central Government” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
267	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE COMMISSIONS OF INQUIRY (SECOND) ORDINANCE, 1958</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE COMMISSIONS OF INQUIRY (SECOND) ORDINANCE, 1958 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. LI OF 1958).[22nd July, 1958]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 WHEREAS by a Proclamation dated the 25th day of June, 1958, under Article 193 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan, the President has assumed to himself all the powers vested in, or exercisable by, the Governor of East Pakistan;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS the President has, in pursuance of sub-clause (i) of clause (c) of the said Proclamation, been pleased to direct by notification No. 22/11/58-Pol. (1), dated the 4th July, 1958, published in the Extraordinary Gazette of Pakistan, dated the 4th July, 1958 that the power vested in or exercisable by the Governor under the Constitution shall be exercised by the Governor;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for the appointment of Commissions of Inquiry and for vesting such Commissions with certain powers;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS the National Assembly is not in session and the Governor is satisfied that circumstances exist which render it necessary for him to take immediate action;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in exercise of the power conferred by Article 102 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Pakistan and of all other powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Short title, extent and commencement</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the 2[ * * *] Commissions of Inquiry (Second) Ordinance, 1958.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of 3[ Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Definitions</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Ordinance unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Commission” means a Commission of Inquiry appointed or deemed to have been appointed under section 3;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “prescribed” means prescribed by rules made under section 12; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “President” means the President of the Commission.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Appointment of Commission</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) The Government may, if it is of opinion that it is necessary so to do, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint a Commission of Inquiry for the purpose of making an inquiry into any definite matter of public importance and performing such functions and within such time as may be specified in the notification, and the Commission so appointed shall make the inquiry and perform the functions accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Commission may consist of one or more members appointed by the Government, and where the Commission consists of more than one member, one of them may be appointed as the President thereof.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Powers of Commission</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. The Commission shall have the powers of a Civil Court, while trying a suit under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, in respect of the following matters, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        summoning and enforcing the attendance of any person and examining him on oath;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) requiring the discovery and production of any documents;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) receiving evidence on affidavits;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) issuing commissions for the examination of witnesses or documents.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Additional powers of Commission</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) Where the Government is of opinion that, having regard to the nature of the inquiry to be made and other circumstances of the case, all or any of the provisions of sub-section (4) or sub-section (5) or sub-section (6) of this section should be made applicable to a Commission, the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, direct that all or such of the said provisions as may be specified in the notification shall apply to that Commission and on the issue of such a notification, the said provisions shall apply accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Commission shall have power to require any person, subject to any privilege which may be claimed by that person under any law for the time being in force, to furnish information on such points or matters as, in the opinion of the Commission, may be useful for, or relevant to, the subject-matter of the inquiry.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The President or any officer, not below the rank of a Gazetted Officer, specially authorised in this behalf by the President, may enter any building or place where the Commission has reason to believe that any books of account or other documents relating to the subject-matter of the inquiry may be found, and may seize any such books of account or documents or take extracts or copies therefrom subject to the provisions of section 102 and section 103 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, in so far as they may be applicable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Commission shall be deemed to be a Civil Court and when any offence as is described in section 175, section 178, section 179, section 180 or section 228 of the 4[ * * *] Penal Code, is committed in the view or presence of the Commission, the Commission may, after recording the facts constituting the offence and the statement of the accused as provided for in the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, forward the case to a Magistrate having jurisdiction to try the same and the Magistrate to whom any such case is forwarded shall proceed to hear the complaint against the accused as if the case had been forwarded to him under section 482 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) Any proceeding before the Commission shall be deemed to be a judicial proceeding within the meaning of sections 193 and 228 of the 5[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) The Commission shall have the powers of a Civil   Court, while trying a suit under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, in respect of requisitioning any public record or copy thereof from any court or office.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Statement made by the persons to the Commission</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. No statement made by a person in the course of giving evidence before the Commission shall subject him to, or be used against him in, any civil or criminal proceeding except a prosecution for giving false evidence by such statement:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that the statement-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) is made in reply to a question which he is required by the Commission to answer; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) is relevant to the subject-matter of inquiry.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Commission to cease to exist when notified</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. The Government may, if it is of opinion that the continued existence of a Commission is unnecessary, by notification in the official Gazette, declare that the Commission shall cease to exist from such date as may be specified in this behalf in such notification, and thereupon, the Commission shall cease to exist.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Procedure to be followed by the Commission</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. The Commission shall, subject to any rules that may be made in this behalf, have power to regulate its own procedure (including the fixing of places and times of its sittings and deciding whether to sit in public or in private) and may act notwithstanding the temporary absence of any member or the existence of a vacancy among its members.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Protection of action taken in good faith</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. No suit or other legal proceedings shall lie against the Government, the Commission or any member thereof, or any person acting under the direction either of the Government or of the Commission in respect of anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done in pursuance of this Ordinance or of any rules or orders made thereunder or in respect of the publication, by or under the authority of the Government or the Commission, of any report, paper or proceedings.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Members, etc, to be public servants</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. Every member of the Commission and every officer appointed or authorised by the Commission to exercise functions under this Ordinance shall be deemed to be a public servant within the meaning of section 21 of the 6[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Ordinance to apply to Inquiry Commissions set up before the promulgation of the Ordinance</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. Where any Commission has been appointed under any Resolution of the Government for the purpose of making an inquiry into any definite matter of public importance before the coming into force of this Ordinance, such Commission shall be deemed to be a Commission appointed under section 3 and the provision of this Ordinance shall apply accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12.       The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules to carry out the purposes of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. [Repealed by Section 3 and the Second Schedule of The East  Pakistan Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1966 (East  Pakistan Ordinance No. XIII of 1966.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the words “East Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The word “Pakistan” was omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The word “Pakistan” was omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word “Pakistan” was omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
268	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE COTTON ACT, 1957 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE COTTON ACT, 1957 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. XXXVIII OF 1957).[10th September, 1957]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide for measures for the promotion of international trade in cotton. 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for measures for the promotion of international trade in cotton;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Cotton Act, 1957</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2[ (2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “contract” means a contract for the purchase or sale of cotton, and includes a factory selection contract;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “cotton” means unginned cotton (kapas) or ginned cotton (rui) or pressed and baled cotton but does not include wool cotton or silk cotton;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “factory selection contract” means a contract for the sale of cotton entered into in Bangladesh and providing for selection by the buyer at the factory and for delivery of the cotton selected in full pressed bales 3[ * * *] within the period and at the price specified in the contract;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        “notified order” means an order published in the official Gazette;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        “pressing factory” means a place wherein steam, water or other mechanical power or electric power is used and where cotton is pressed into bales.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Constitution of the Cotton Board</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4[ 3. (1) The Government may, for the promotion of international trade in cotton, constitute, by notification in the official Gazette, a Cotton Board with a Chairman and such other members, not exceeding ten, as may be specified in the notification.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Chairman and the members of the Cotton Board shall be nominated by the Government.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Functions of the Board</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. The Board shall have power to supervise and regulate all dealings in cotton, in so far as they are connected with the promotion of international trade therein, and shall perform such functions as the Government may, from time to time, direct for the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Control of the Board</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. The Board shall be subject to the superintendence and control of the Government, and in the discharge of its functions shall be guided by such general or special instructions as may, from time to time, be given to it by the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. [Requisition of factories, etc.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to secure fulfilment of contracts</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. If in the opinion of the Government, it is expedient or necessary so to do for the purpose of securing the fulfilment of any contract relating to export of cotton on which the exporter has defaulted, it may buy cotton elsewhere and appropriate it to the contract, and the defaulter shall be liable for any loss which the Government may sustain on that account, but the defaulter shall not be entitled to any gain on the purchase made against default.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- In this section “exporter” means a seller of cotton to a foreign buyer or to his agent in Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to call for information</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. (1) The Government may, at any time, by an order in writing, direct such person or class of persons as may be specified in the order to furnish such particulars relating to the fulfilment of any contract relating to export of cotton, in such manner and to such person, as may be specified in the order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may, by order in writing, require any person to furnish to it, or to such person as may be specified in this order, any information in his possession, being information which the Government may require for the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Registration of contracts</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. The Government may, by general or special order in writing, require any contract relating to export of cotton to be registered with such organisation and in such manner as may be specified in the order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Control of contracts through recognised associations</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. (1) The Government, if satisfied that it could be in the interests of the trade and also of the public to do so, may, by a notified order and subject to such conditions, if any, as may be specified in the order, prohibit any specified kind or class of contracts, such as forward contracts or hedge contracts, unless such contracts are made through and under the control of, and in the manner prescribed by, an association recognised by the Government under sub-section (2).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) For the purposes of this section, the Government may, by a notified order, recognise any association, constituted for the purpose of regulating and controlling contracts, which applies for such recognition.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) A recognition under sub-section (2) may be granted subject to the condition that the association shall by such amendments of its articles of association, rules or bye-laws as may be necessary provide for the appointment by the Government of not more than four persons, representing interests not directly represented through membership of the association, as members of the governing body of the association.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) Every association, which is recognised under sub-section (2), shall furnish to the Government such information and such periodical returns relating to the affairs of the association as the Government may by order in writing require.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) The Government may, by order in writing, give such directions, as it considers necessary in the interests of the trade and the public, to an association recognised under sub-section (2) in respect of contracts to which this section applies.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) No articles, rules or bye-laws of an association recognised under sub-section (2) shall be altered save with the previous approval of the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7) Whenever the Government considers it expedient to do so, it may by order in writing, direct any association recognised under sub-section (2) to make, repeal or amend any articles, rules or bye-laws of the association in the manner and within a period specified in the order; and if the recognised association refuses, fails or neglects to comply with the direction within the specified period, the Government may, by a notified order, make, repeal or amend the articles, rules or bye-laws in the manner specified in the order giving the direction or with such modifications as the Government may think fit, and the making, repeal or amendment of the articles, rules or bye-laws shall be deemed to have been duly effected by the association.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8) If the Government is of the opinion that the interests of the trade and the public require that the recognition accorded to an association under sub-section (2) should be terminated, the Government may, after giving the association a reasonable opportunity of being heard in the matter, by a notified order, terminate the recognition on and from the date of such order or any specified date subsequent thereto, and the association shall cease to be an association recognised under sub-section (2) from the date of such termination:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that such termination shall not affect the validity of any contract entered into or made before the date of such termination.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Delegation of powers</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. The Government may, by a notified order, direct that any power conferred upon it by or under this Act shall, in relation to such matters and subject to such conditions, if any, as may be specified in the order, be exercisable by the Cotton Board.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Penalty etc</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. (1) Any person who contravenes or fails to comply with an order made or direction given under this Act shall be punishable as if he had contravened a provision of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Any person who contravenes any provision of this Act shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Where any person as aforesaid is a company or a body corporate, every director, manager, secretary or other officer, and every agent and servant thereof, and in the case of an unlimited company or a company limited by guarantee, also any of its members, shall, subject to the provisions of the next succeeding sub-section, be punishable as if he had contravened the provisions of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) No such director, manager, secretary or other officer and no such agent, servant or member as is referred to in sub-section (3) shall be prosecuted under this Act unless he has been given an opportunity by the Government to show cause, within such time as the Government may specify, why he should not be prosecuted, and if it is made to appear to the satisfaction of the Government at any time before the institution of the prosecution that he has used due diligence to enforce the observance of the provisions of this Act and the orders and directions issued thereunder and that the offence has been committed without his knowledge or against his consent, the Government may
