forbear further proceedings against him:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that nothing in this sub-section shall prevent the Government from proceeding against him further if it sees reason to do so.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">False Statements</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. If any person-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         when required by an order under this Act to make any statement or furnish any information, makes any statement or furnishes any information which is false in any material particular and which he knows or has reasonable cause to believe to be false, or does not believe to be true, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        makes any such statement as aforesaid in any book, account, record, declaration, return or other documents which he is required by any such order to maintain or furnish,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">14. (1) The Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power, such rules may prescribe the procedure for determining, whether by means of arbitration or otherwise, the loss that may be sustained by Government in securing the fulfilment of any contract on which an exporter has defaulted, and the manner in which the liability of the defaulter for such loss may be discharged by him.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Rules made under this section shall be laid before the National Assembly at its meeting held next after the publication of the notification under sub-section (1).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Cognizance of offences</p><p style="text-align: justify;">15. No court shall take cognizance of any offence punishable under this Act except on a report in writing of the facts constituting such offence made by a person who is a public servant as defined in section 21 of the 5[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Special provision regarding fines</p><p style="text-align: justify;">16. Notwithstanding anything contained in section 32 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, it shall be lawful for any Magistrate of the First Class specially empowered by the 6[ Government] in this behalf to pass a sentence of fine exceeding one thousand 7[ taka] on any person convicted under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Presumption as to orders</p><p style="text-align: justify;">17. Where an order purports to have been made and signed by an authority in exercise of any power conferred by or under this Act, a court shall, within the meaning of the Evidence Act, 1872, presume that such order was so made by that authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">18. [Repeal.-Repealed by Section 2 and 1st Schedule of the Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1965 (Ordinance No. X of 1965).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, unless otherwise provided, the word “Bangladesh” and “Government” were substituted for the words “Pakistan” and “Central Government” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 Sub-section (2) was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The words “at Karachi” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 Section 3 was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The word “Pakistan” was omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government ” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The word “taka” was substituted for the word “rupees” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
269	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE COTTON GINNING AND PRESSING ACT, 1957 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE COTTON GINNING AND PRESSING ACT, 1957 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(EAST PAKISTAN ACT NO. XIII OF 1957).[7th May, 1957]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An  Act to provide for powers to regulate charges for ginning and pressing of cotton, to requisition factories for storing of cotton and to enforce any agreement for the purchase and sale of cotton. 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for powers to control the charges for ginning and pressing of cotton, requisition of factories for storage of cotton and other incidental matters;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1.         (1) This Act may be called the 2[ * * *] Cotton Ginning and Pressing Act, 1957.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of 3[ Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) This Act shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Cotton” means unginned cotton (kapas) or ginned cotton (rui) or pressed and baled cotton, but does not include wool cotton or silk cotton;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “Factory” means a place wherein steam, water or other mechanical power or electric power is used and where-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         cotton is ginned or where cotton fibre is separated from cotton seed, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        cotton is pressed into bales;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “Factory Selection Contract” means a contract for the sale of cotton 4[ * * *] and providing for selection by the buyer at the factory and for delivery of the cotton selected in full pressed bales at Chittagong within the period and at the price specified in the contract; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        “Occupier” means an occupier of a factory as owner, allottee, lessee or manager.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Ginning and pressing charges</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. The Government may, by a notified order, regulate the charges to be made for the ginning and pressing of cotton and such order may regulate such charges uniformly in respect of all areas and factories or differentially in respect of particular areas or factories.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Requisition of factories, etc</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) The Government may, by a general or special order, requisition any factory or any place, whether open or enclosed, and use the same for ginning, pressing or storing cotton and for purposes incidental to the purposes of this Act, whether such cotton has been purchased by or on behalf of the Government or not.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If any such factory or place is requisitioned under this section, there shall be paid compensation which shall be determined in the manner and in accordance with the principles hereinafter set out, that is to say-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        where the amount of compensation can be fixed by agreement, it shall be paid in accordance with such agreement;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        where no such agreement can be reached, the Government shall appoint as arbitrator a person qualified for appointment as a Judge of 5[ the High Court Division];</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        the Government may, in any case, nominate a person having expert knowledge as to the nature of the factory or place requisitioned, to assist the arbitrator, and where such nomination is made, the person to be compensated may also nominate an assessor for the said purpose;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        at the commencement of the proceedings before the arbitrator, the Government and the person to be compensated shall state what, in their respective opinions, is a fair amount of compensation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        the arbitrator in making his award shall have regard to the provisions of 6[ sub-section (1) of section 8 of the Acquisition and Requisition of Immovable Property Ordinance, 1982 (II of 1982)], so far as the same can be made applicable to an acquisition of a temporary character.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The Government may prescribe the procedure to be followed in arbitration under sub-section (2).</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Proprietors, etc, of ginning factories to buy cotton offered for sale</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) Where cotton is offered for sale to the occupier of a ginning factory, he shall buy the same and pay a price for it not less than the minimum price fixed for such cotton under any law for the time being in force.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) If he fails to buy the cotton so offered to him or buys it at a price below the minimum price referred to in sub-section (1), then without prejudice to any punishment which may be imposed on him for having contravened a provision of this Act, the Government may order that the factory of which he is the occupier shall be confiscated to the Government and worked thereafter in such manner as it may see fit to direct.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) He shall be at liberty after having bought the said cotton to sell the same to any person or at his option to the Government in accordance with the terms of an agreement to be entered into between him and the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) If after having entered into such agreement he contravenes or fails to comply with any provision of the same, he shall, without prejudice to any other action which the Government may take against him under this Act or under any other law for the time being in force, be deemed to have contravened a provision of this Act, and shall be punishable accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Penalty</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) Any person who contravenes or fails to comply with an order made or a direction given under this Act shall be punishable as if he had contravened a provision of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Any person who contravenes any provision of this Act shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to 3 years or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Where any person as aforesaid is company or other body corporate, every member, director, manager, secretary or other officer and every agent and servant thereof shall be punishable as if he had contravened a provision of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) No person shall be prosecuted under this Act unless he has been given an opportunity by the Government to show cause within such time as the Government may specify why he should not be prosecuted, and if it is made to appear to the satisfaction of the Government at any time before the institution of the prosecution that he has used due diligence to enforce the observance of the provisions of this Act and that the offence has been committed without his knowledge or against his consent, the Government may forbear further proceedings against him:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that nothing in this sub-section shall prevent the Government from proceeding against him further if it sees reason to do so, in which case he shall not be prosecuted unless he has been given a further opportunity as aforesaid.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Attempts and abetments</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. Any person who attempts to contravene, or abets a contravention of, any provision of this Act or any order made or direction given thereunder, shall be deemed to have contravened that provision, order or direction.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">False statement</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. If any person-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         when required by an order under this Act to make any statement or furnish any information makes any statement or furnishes any information which is false in any material particular and which he knows or has reasonable cause to believe to be false or does not believe to be true, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        makes any statement as aforesaid in any book, account, record, declaration, return or other document which he is required by any such order to maintain or furnish,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to 3 years or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Cognizance of offence</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. No Court shall take cognizance of any offence punishable under this Act except on a report in writing of the facts constituting such offence made by a person who is a public servant as defined in section 21 of the 7[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to try offences summarily</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10.       Any Magistrate or Bench of Magistrate empowered for the time being to try in a summary way the offence specified in sub-section (1) of section 260 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898 may, on application in this behalf being made by the prosecution, try in accordance with the provision contained in sections 260 and 265 of the said Code any offence punishable under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Special provision regarding fines</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11.       Notwithstanding anything contained in section 32 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, it shall be lawful for any Magistrate of the First Class specially empowered by the Government in this behalf to pass a sentence of fine exceeding one thousand 8[ taka] on any person convicted under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Presumption as to orders</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12.       (1) No order made in exercise of any power conferred by or under this Act shall be called in question in any Court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where an order purports to have been made and signed by an authority in exercise of any power conferred by or under this Act, a Court shall, within the meaning of the Evidence Act, 1872, presume that such order was so made by that authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Protection of action taken under this Act</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13.       No suit, prosecution or other legal proceeding shall lie in respect of anything which is, in good faith, done or intended to be done in pursuance of any order made under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the words “East Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “entered into in East Pakistan” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The words “the High Court Division” were substituted for the words “a High Court” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The words, brackets, figures and comma “sub-section (1) of section 8 of the Acquisition and Requisition of Immovable Property Ordinance, 1982 (II of 1982)” were substituted for the words, brackets, figures and comma “sub-section (1) of section 23 of the Land Acquisition Act, 1894” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The word “Pakistan” was omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8 The word “taka” was substituted for the word “rupees” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
270	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE CULTURABLE WASTE LAND (UTILIZATION) ORDINANCE, 1959 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE CULTURABLE WASTE LAND (UTILIZATION) ORDINANCE, 1959</strong></p><p align="center">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. XIII OF 1959)</p><p align="right">[26th January, 1959]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is necessary to bring under cultivation culturable waste land with a view to step up production of food;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Presidential Proclamation of the 7th day of October, 1958, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the Culturable Waste Land (Utilization) Ordinance, 1959.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1[ (2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh but shall not apply to any urban area within the meaning of the Paurashava Ordinance, 1977 (Ordinance No. XXVI of 1977)].</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Ordinance, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i)         “Deputy Commissioner” used in relation to any culturable waste land, means the Deputy Commissioner of the district within which such culturable waste land is situated and includes any officer 2[ * * *] appointed by the Deputy Commissioner to carry out all or any of the functions of a Deputy Commissioner under this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        “food crops” include vegetables and fruits;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(iii)       “culturable waste land” means any land classified in the record-of-rights published under 3[ * * *] the 4[ * * *] State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950, as nutan patit, purantan patit, layek patit, garlayek patit or layek jangal and includes any land which, in the opinion of the Deputy Commissioner, has not been cultivated during the last two preceding years and no preparation for its cultivation has been made on the day of making a declaration under section 3, but does not include land forming part of, or conterminous with, any homestead, farm-house or any place of worship.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Application of the provisions of this Ordinance to culturable waste land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. The Deputy Commissioner may declare that the provisions of this Ordinance shall apply to any culturable waste land and on and from the day of making such declaration the possession of such culturable waste land shall vest in the Deputy Commissioner for a period not exceeding one year, and where the culturable waste land would, in the opinion of the Deputy Commissioner, require substantial reclamation, for a period not exceeding ten years, from the date of such declaration:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that no such subsequent declaration for any year shall be made more than three months in advance or for a period of more than one year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Lease of culturable waste land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. When the possession of any culturable waste land has vested in the Deputy Commissioner, he may lease it out on such terms and conditions as he thinks proper to any person or persons for purpose of cultivation for production of food crops for the period for which the possession has vested in the Deputy Commissioner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Compensation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) Whenever a declaration is made under section 3, the owner of the culturable waste land, in respect of which the declaration has been made, shall, for the period during which the possession of the culturable waste land remains vested in the Deputy Commissioner, be paid an annual compensation equivalent to the amount of the annual rent or land revenue payable in respect of such land.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No person shall be entitled to claim any compensation from the Deputy Commissioner, for leasing out any culturable waste land to any other person under section 4.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Right of lessees over waste land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. Notwithstanding anything contained in any other law for the time being in force no person to whom the Deputy Commissioner leases out any culturable waste land shall acquire any right, title or interest whatsoever therein beyond the period for which it has been leased out.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Possession of culturable waste land</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. (1) Where the owner wishes to cultivate himself the culturable waste land, in respect of which a declaration has been made under section 3, after the expiry of the period for which the possession has vested in the Deputy Commissioner, he may, not later than three months before the expiry of the period, serve a notice on the Deputy Commissioner to that effect accompanied by security deposit of 5[ Tk] 50 per acre and in such case such land shall be released by the Deputy Commissioner at the end of the above mentioned period and the possession thereof shall vest back in the owner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where the owner of the culturable waste land, of which possession has vested back in such owner under sub-section (1), fails to cultivate such land and raise any crop therein after possession thereof has so vested back, such culturable waste land together with the security deposit under sub-section (1) shall be forfeited to the 6[ Government].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bar to jurisdiction of Court</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. No declaration made by the Deputy Commissioner in pursuance of the provision of this Ordinance and no order made by him for leasing out any culturable waste land shall be called in question in any Court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Rule-making power</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. The 7[ Government] may make rules for carrying out the purposes of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_____________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Sub-section (2) was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “not below the rank of a Subdivisional Magistrate” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The words, commas, figures and brackets “the Bengal Tenancy Act, 1885 (Ben. Act VIII of 1885), or” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The word “Tk” was substituted for the word “Rs” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
271	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE DHANMANDAI RESIDENTIAL ZONE (TERMINATION OF LEASE) ORDINANCE, 1959 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE DHANMANDAI RESIDENTIAL ZONE (TERMINATION OF LEASE) ORDINANCE, 1959</strong></p><p align="center">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. LXXVI OF 1959)</p><p align="right">[7th December, 1959]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS the Government have leased out plots of Dhanmandai Residential Area to the tenants on terms and conditions set forth in the Standard Agreement for Dhanmandai Residential Area;   1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is provided in the Indenture of Agreement executed by the tenants that the construction of houses, out-houses and appurtenances on the demised property shall be made within 2 years from the date of commencement of the lease or within such further time as the Government may allow in its discretion;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is further provided that on the failure of the tenant to complete the construction of house, out-houses and appurtenances within the aforesaid period or within such time as the Government may allow, the lease shall be liable to be terminated by the Government and on such termination, the tenant shall surrender the demised property to the Government forthwith;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS some such tenant has obtained allotment of more than one plot in the name of his wife, husband or children;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">AND WHEREAS it is expedient to remove any doubt as to the power of the Government to terminate any such lease and to take over possession of the demised property for failure of the tenant to complete the construction within the period stipulated in the Indenture of Lease and for allotment of more than one plot in the family;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Presidential Proclamation of the seventh day of October, 1958, and in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor</p><p style="text-align: justify;">of East Pakistan is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Short title and commencement</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the Dhanmandai Residential Zone (Termination of Lease) Ordinance, 1959.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bar to jurisdiction of Civil Courts</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. When the Government terminates any lease in respect of any plot in the Dhanmandai Residential Area, on the failure of the tenant to complete the constructions of the houses, out-houses and appurtenances within the period stipulated in the Indenture of Lease and for allotment of more than one plot in the family and takes possession of the same, no suit or proceeding of any kind whatsoever shall lie or be proceeded with in any Court to challenge the validity of any such order of termination of the lease and taking over possession of the demised property on the termination of such lease.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- ‘Family' means husband, wife and children.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_______________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p>                       </div></div>
272	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE DIPLOMATIC IMMUNITIES (COMMONWEALTH COUNTRIES REPRESENTATIVES) ACT, 1957 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE DIPLOMATIC IMMUNITIES (COMMONWEALTH COUNTRIES REPRESENTATIVES) ACT, 1957 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. XXIX OF 1957).[30th April, 1957]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An  Act to declare and confer certain immunities on representatives in Bangladesh of Commonwealth Countries and on certain other persons. 1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to declare and confer certain immunities upon representatives in Bangladesh of Commonwealth Countries and on certain other persons and to provide for certain other matters;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Diplomatic Immunities (Commonwealth Countries Representatives) Act, 1957.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “chief representative” means a person whether known by the title of High Commissioner or by any other title, who for the time being is recognised by the Government of Bangladesh as the chief representative in Bangladesh of a Commonwealth Country for the purposes of this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “envoy” means the envoy of a foreign sovereign power duly accredited in Bangladesh;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “member of the family” of a person means his wife and his unmarried children below the age of twenty one, when resident with him;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        “prescribed” means prescribed by rules made under this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        “staff” of a chief representative includes every person employed by the chief representative but not servants employed by a member of the staff;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         “the official staff” of a chief representative means officials employed in a representative capacity directly under the orders of the chief representative.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Immunity of chief representative</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. A chief representative is and shall be entitled to the immunity from suit and legal process, and to the inviolability of residence, official premises and official archives, to which he would be entitled if he were an envoy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Immunity of member of staff or family</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) Subject to sub-section (2) a person who is,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        a member of the family of a chief representative,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        a member of the staff of a chief representative, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) a member of the family of a member of the official staff of a chief representative,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">is and shall be entitled to the immunity from suit and legal process to which he would be entitled if the chief representative were an envoy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) When a person who is a member of the staff of a chief representative is or is deemed to be a citizen of Bangladesh-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        that person is and shall be entitled to immunity under this Act only in respect of things done or omitted to be done in the course of the performance of his duties as a member of that staff; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        a member of the family of that person is not by reason only of his being a member of that family entitled to any immunity under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Rules for grant of consular immunity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. The 2[ Government] may make rules providing that any person who holds any prescribed office in the service of the Government of a prescribed part of the Commonwealth shall, on being recognised by the Government of Bangladesh in the prescribed manner as a person entitled to the immunity from suit and legal process and to the inviolability of official premises and official archives to which he would be entitled if he were a consular officer of a foreign sovereign power, be so entitled.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Waiver of Immunity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) A chief representative may waive any right to immunity or inviolability to which-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        he or a member of his family,</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        a member of his staff, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        a member of the family of a member of his official staff may be entitled under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A person may waive any right to immunity or inviolability which has been conferred on him under the rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Certificate regarding immunity</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. (1) The Government may issue in the prescribed manner a certificate certifying any fact relevant to the question whether a person is or is not entitled under this Act or the rules made thereunder to immunity from suit or legal process or to inviolability of residence, official premises or official archives.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A certificate issued under sub-section (1) shall be conclusive evidence in any legal proceedings of the facts certified in the certificate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. (1) The 3[ Government] may make rules for the purpose of carrying out the purposes of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing power the rules may provide that, if the 4[ Government] is of the opinion that persons representing Bangladesh in any country within the Commonwealth are not accorded treatment corresponding to the treatment accorded to persons representing that country in Bangladesh, the recognition of any representative of that country for the purposes of this Act and the immunities and inviolabilities to which the representatives or other persons of that country are otherwise entitled under this Act or the rules made thereunder shall cease, or that the immunities and inviolabilities shall be curtailed to the extent and in the manner prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the word “Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The word “Government” was substituted for the word “President” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Government” was substituted for the word “President” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The word “Government” was substituted for the word “President” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
273	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE ESSENTIAL COMMODITIES ACT, 1957 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE ESSENTIAL COMMODITIES ACT, 1957 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ACT NO. III OF 1957).[6th March, 1957]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Act to provide for price control and regulation of trade and commerce 1[ between different areas in Bangladesh in respect of certain commodities].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to provide for price control and regulation of trade and commerce 2[ between different areas in Bangladesh] in respect of certain commodities;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is hereby enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the Essential Commodities Act, 1957.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of 3[ Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force at once.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> Definitions </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Act, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4[ * * *]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “essential commodity” means any of the classes of commodities mentioned in the Schedule to this Act, and such other classes of commodities as may be declared by the 5[ Government] by notification in the official Gazette to be essential commodities for the purposes of this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “notified order” means an order notified in the official Gazette.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power to make orders, etc</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. 6[ (1) The Government, so far as it appears to it to be necessary or expedient for securing the equitable distribution of an essential commodity between different areas in Bangladesh and availability at fair prices or for promoting export thereof, may, by notified order, provide for regulating the production, movement, transport and sale of the essential commodity in different areas in Bangladesh and for the prices to be charged or paid for it at any stage of the transaction therein.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Without prejudice to the generality of the powers conferred by sub-section (1), an order made thereunder may provide-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        for controlling the prices at which any essential commodity may be bought or sold in any area;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7[ (aa) for procuring any essential commodity for purposes of export;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(aaa) for regulating, restricting or prohibiting the sale, disposal, transport and movement of any essential commodity within 8[ different areas in Bangladesh], for purposes of such procurement;]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        for regulating by licences, permits or otherwise, the transport, movement and distribution 9[ between different areas in Bangladesh] of an essential commodity;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        for prohibiting the withholding of sale 10[ between different areas in Bangladesh] of an essential commodity ordinarily kept for sale;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) for requiring any person holding stock 11[ in an area in Bangladesh an essential commodity to sell in another area thereof] the whole or specific part of the stock at such price to such persons or class of persons under such circumstances as may be specified in the order;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) for collecting any information or statistics with a view to regulating or prohibiting any of the aforesaid matters;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f) for requiring persons engaged in any of the matters mentioned above in respect of any essential commodity to maintain and produce for inspection such books, accounts and records relating to their business and to furnish such information relating thereto as may be specified in the order;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g) for any incidental and supplementary matters, including in particular the entering, and search of premises, vehicles, vessels and aircraft, the seizure by a person authorised to make such search of any articles in respect of which such person has reason to believe that a contravention of the order has been, is being or is about to be committed, or any records connected therewith, the grant or issue of licences, permits or other documents, and the charging of fees therefore.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. [Delegation of powers.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Delegation of powers by Government</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12[ 4A. The 13[ Government] may delegate any of its powers under section 3 to any of its officers, by an order notified in the official Gazette, subject to such conditions as may be specified in the order.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Effect of orders inconsistent with other enactments</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. Any order made under section 3 shall have effect notwithstanding anything inconsistent therewith contained in any enactment other than this Act or any instrument having effect by virtue of any enactment other than this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Penalties</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) If any person contravenes any order made under section 3, he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine or with both, and if the order so provides, any Court trying such contravention may direct that any property in respect of which the Court is satisfied that the order has been contravened shall be forfeited to the 14[ Government]:</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that where the contravention is of an order relating to foodstuffs which contains an express provision in this behalf, the Court shall make such direction, unless for reasons to be recorded in writing it is of opinion that the direction should not be made in respect of the whole, or, as the case may be, a part, of the property.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The owner of any vessel, conveyance or animal carrying any property in respect of which an order under section 3 is contravened shall, if the carrying is part of the transaction involving the contravention and if he knew or had reason to believe that the contravention was being committed, be deemed to have contravened the order, and in addition to the punishment to which he is liable under sub-section (1) the vessel, conveyance or animal shall, when the order provides for forfeiture of the property in respect of which the order is contravened, be forfeited to the 15[ Government].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Attempts and abetments</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. Any person who attempts to contravene, or abets a contravention of, any order made under section 3 shall be deemed to have contravened that order.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Offences by Corporations</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. If the person contravening an order made under section 3 is a company or other body corporate, every director, manager, secretary or other officer or agent thereof shall, unless he proves that the contravention took place without his knowledge or that he exercised all due diligence to prevent such contravention, be deemed to be guilty of such contravention.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">False statements</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. If any person-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) when required by an order made under section 3 to make any statement or furnish any information makes any statement or furnishes any information which is false in any material particular and which he knows or has reasonable cause to believe to be false, or does not believe to be true, or</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(ii)        makes any statement as aforesaid in any book, account, record, declaration, return or other document which he is required by any such order to maintain or furnish;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">he shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to three years or with fine or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Cognizance of offences</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. No Court shall take cognizance of any offence punishable under this Act except on a report in writing of the facts constituting such offence made by a person who is a public servant as defined in section 21 of the 16[ * * *] Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Powers to try offences summarily</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. Any magistrate or bench of magistrates empowered for the time being to try in a summary way the offences specified in sub-section (1) of section 260 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, may, on application in this behalf being made by the prosecution, try in accordance with the provisions contained in sections 262 to 265 of the said Code any offence punishable under this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Special provision regarding fines</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. Notwithstanding anything contained in section 32 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898, it should be lawful for any Magistrate of the First Class specially empowered by the 17[ Government] in this behalf to pass a sentence of fine exceeding one thousand 18[ taka] on any person convicted of contravening an order made under section 3.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Presumption as to order</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. (1) No order made in exercise of any power conferred by or under this Act shall be called in question in any Court.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Where an order purports to have been made and signed by an authority in exercise of any power conferred by or under this Act, a Court shall, within the meaning of the Evidence Act, 1872, presume that such order was so made by that authority.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Burden of proof in certain cases</p><p style="text-align: justify;">14. Where any person is prosecuted for contravening any order made under section 3 which prohibits him from doing an act or being in possession of a thing without lawful authority or without a permit, licence or other document, the burden of proving that he has such authority, permit, licence or other document, shall be on him.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Protection of action taken under the Act</p><p style="text-align: justify;">15. (1) No suit, prosecution or other legal proceeding shall lie against any person for anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done in pursuance of any order made under section 3.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No suit or other legal proceeding shall lie against Government for any damage caused or likely to be caused by anything which is in good faith done or intended to be done in pursuance of any order made under section 3.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">19[ Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">16. [Repeal.- Repealed by section 2 and 1st Schedule of the Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1965 (Ordinance No. X of 1965).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 The words “between different areas in Bangladesh in respect of certain commodities” were substituted for the words “between the Provinces” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “between different areas in Bangladesh” were substituted for the words “between the Provinces and between different areas in a Province” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the word “Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 Clause (a1) was omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “appropriate Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 Sub-section (1) was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 Clauses (aa) and (aaa) were inserted by section 4 of the Essential Supplies (Amendment) Ordinance, 1962 (Ordinance No. IV of 1962)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8 The words “different areas in Bangladesh” were substituted for the words “a Province or in different areas in a Province” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9 The words “between different areas in Bangladesh” were substituted for the words “between the Provinces or between different areas in a Province” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10 The words “between different areas in Bangladesh” were substituted for the words “between the Provinces or between different areas in a Province” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">11 The words the same Province” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align:
