sale of the properties pledged, mortgaged, hypothecated or assigned by the borrower as security for the loan;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        an injunction restraining the borrower from in any manner removing, transferring or disposing of any of the properties referred to in clause (a); and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        an ad interim attachment attaching the properties referred to in clause (a) above and such other properties of the borrower as in the opinion of the Court may be sufficient to cover the claim of the Corporation against the borrower.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The plaint under sub-section (1) shall be in the prescribed form and shall state the nature and extent of the liability of the borrower to the Corporation, the grounds upon which it is made and such other particulars as may be prescribed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Save as otherwise provided by this section, the Code of the Civil Procedure, 1908, shall so far as may be applicable to the proceedings on such a plaint.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The borrower shall not appear to defend the suit unless he obtains leave from the Court as hereinafter provided so to appear and defend; and in default of his obtaining such leave or of his appearance and defence in pursuance thereof, the allegations in the plaint shall be deemed to be admitted and the Corporation shall be entitled to decree accordingly.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) If the borrower discloses such facts upon affidavit or otherwise as in the opinion of the Court are sufficient to entitle him to appear and defend the suit, the Court shall grant him leave to appear and defend. Such leave may be granted unconditionally or subject to such terms as to payment into Court, giving security framing and recording of issues or otherwise as the Court thinks fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) A decree passed under this section may be executed forthwith.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7) After the decree the Court may under special circumstances set aside the decree and, if necessary, stay or set aside execution and may give leave to the borrower to appear and defend the suit if it seems reasonable to the Court so to do, and on such terms as the Court thinks fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8) A decree passed under this section shall be appealable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Act XVIII of 1891 to apply to the books of the Corporation</p><p style="text-align: justify;">35. The Corporation shall be deemed to be a Bank for the purpose of the Banker's Book Evidence Act, 1891.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Disposal of profit</p><p style="text-align: justify;">36. After making provision for bad and doubtful debits, depreciation of assets and any other matters which are usually provided for by bankers, the Corporation shall, out of its net annual profit, establish a Reserve Fund and may declare a dividend.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The rate of such dividend shall not exceed five per centum per annum.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">General meetings</p><p style="text-align: justify;">37. (1) A general meeting (hereinafter referred to as the annual general meeting) shall be held at the office of the Corporation annually within two months from the date on which the annual accounts of the Corporation are closed and a general meeting may be convened by the Board at any other time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The shareholders present at the annual general meeting shall be entitled to discuss the annual accounts, the annual report of the Board on the working of the Corporation and the auditors' report on the annual balance sheet and accounts, and to express their views in the form of resolutions; and the Corporation shall consider such views and give such effect to them as it considers fit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Audit</p><p style="text-align: justify;">38.       (1) The accounts of the Corporation shall be audited by not less than two auditors holding a certificate under 12[ section 212 of the Companies Act, 1994 (Act 18 of 1994)], who shall be appointed by the Government on such remuneration as it may fix, and such remuneration shall be paid by the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Every auditor appointed under sub-section (1) shall be given a copy of the annual balance sheet of the Corporation, and shall examine it together with the accounts and vouchers relating thereto, and shall have a list delivered to him of all books kept by the Corporation, and shall at all reasonable times have access to the books, accounts and other documents of the Corporation, and may in relation to such accounts examine any Director or Officer of the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The auditors shall report to the shareholders upon the annual balance sheet and accounts and in their report they shall state whether in their opinion the balance sheet exhibits a true and correct view of the state of the Corporation's affairs according to the best of their information and the explanations given to them and as shown by the books of the Corporation, and whether in their opinion books of accounts have been kept by the Corporation in a proper manner and, in case they have called for any explanation or information from the Board, whether it has been given and whether it is satisfactory.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) The Government may at any time issue directions to the auditors requiring them to report to it upon the adequacy of the measures taken by the Corporation for the protection of interests of its shareholders and creditors or upon the sufficiency of their procedure in auditing the affairs of the Corporation, and may at any time enlarge or extend the scope of the audit or direct that a different procedure in audit be adopted or that any other examination be made by the auditor if in its opinion the public interest so requires.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Returns</p><p style="text-align: justify;">39. (1) The Corporation shall furnish to all shareholders within ten days of the date to which the statement relates, a statement in the prescribed form of its assets and liabilities as they stand at the close of business on the last Thursday of each month, or if that day is a public holiday under the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881, then as they stand at the close of business on the preceding working day.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Corporation shall furnish in the prescribed form to the Government such returns and statements at such intervals as the Government may require from time to time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The Corporation shall furnish to the Government within two months of the close of the financial year an audited statement in the prescribed form of its assets and liabilities as they stand at the close of that year together with a profit and loss account for the year and a report on the working of the Corporation during the year, and copies of the said statement, account and report shall be published in the official Gazette and shall be laid before 13[ Parliament].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Liquidation of Corporation</p><p style="text-align: justify;">40. No provision of law relating to the winding up of companies or corporations shall apply to the Corporation and the Corporation shall not be wound up save by order of the Government and in such manner as it may direct.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Indemnity of Directors</p><p style="text-align: justify;">41. (1) Every Director shall be indemnified by the Corporation against all losses and expenses incurred by him in the discharge of his duties except such as are caused by his own wilful act or default.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) A Director shall not be personally responsible for the acts of any other Director or of any officer or servant of the Corporation for any loss or expense resulting to the Corporation by reason of the insufficiency or deficiency in value of or title to any property or security acquired or taken on behalf of the Corporation or by the wrongful act of any person under a liability to the Corporation, or by anything done by him in good faith in the execution of the duties of his office.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Declaration of fidelity and secrecy</p><p style="text-align: justify;">42.       Every Director, auditor, officer or servant of the Corporation shall, before entering upon his duties, make a declaration of fidelity and secrecy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provision relating to income-tax and super-tax</p><p style="text-align: justify;">43.       For the purposes of the 14[ Income-tax Ordinance, 1984 (XXXVI of 1984)], the Corporation shall be deemed to be a company within the meaning of that Act, and shall be liable to income-tax and super-tax accordingly on its income, profits and gains.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Offences</p><p style="text-align: justify;">44.       (1) Whoever wilfully makes a false statement or knowingly makes use of any false statement for the purpose of obtaining a loan from the Corporation or of inducing the Corporation to accept any security in any form or kind shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to two years, or with a fine which may extend to two thousand taka, or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Whoever being a member of the Board or of any Committee of the Corporation discloses or uses for a purpose not connected with the discharge of his duties as a member of the Board or of such Committee any information supplied to the Corporation or to the Board or to the Committee by a person applying for financial assistance shall be punishable with imprisonment for a term which may extend to six months, or with fine which may extend to one thousand taka, or with both.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) No Court shall take cognizance of any offence punishable under this Act otherwise than on a complaint in writing signed by an officer of the Corporation authorised by the Board in this behalf.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power of Government to make rules</p><p style="text-align: justify;">45.       The Government may make rules not inconsistent with this Act for the purpose of giving effect to the provisions of this Act, and where the regulations framed under the next succeeding section are inconsistent with the rules, the rules shall prevail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power of the Board to make regulations</p><p style="text-align: justify;">46.       (1) The Board may, with the previous sanction of the Government, make regulations not inconsistent with this Act or the rules made under this Act to provide for all matters for which provision is necessary or expedient for the purpose of giving effect to the provisions of this Act.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing powers, such regulations may provide for-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the holding and conduct of elections under this Act including the final decision of doubts or disputes regarding the validity of elections;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the manner in which and the conditions subject to which the first allotment of the shares of the Corporation shall be made;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the manner in which and the conditions subject to which the shares of the Corporation may be held and transferred and generally all matters relating to the rights and duties of the shareholders;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        the manner in which the general meeting shall be convened, the procedure to be followed thereat, and the manner in which the right to vote may be exercised;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e)        the calling of the meetings of the Board and of the Executive Committee, fees for attending the meeting thereof and the conduct of business thereat;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(f)         the manner and terms of issue and redemption of bonds and debentures by the Corporation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(g)        the conditions subject to which the Corporation may grant loans;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(h)        the form and manner of determining the sufficiency of the security taken under section 26;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(i) the manner in which and the conditions subject to which the Corporation may borrow in foreign currency from foreign lenders;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(j) the form of returns and statements required under this Act;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(k)        the terms and conditions of service, duties and conduct of officers and servants and agents of the Corporation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(l) the disclosure of interest, direct or indirect, of a Director of the Board in any application for loan;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(m)       the taking over of, and the management of the business of a subsidiary corporation or a company or co-operative society committing a breach of its agreement with the Corporation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(n)        the preparation of annual estimates of income and expenditure of the Corporation in the prescribed form and their submission to the Board and the Government for approval on prescribed dates; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(o)        the efficient conduct of the affairs of the Corporation generally.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) All regulations made under this section shall be published in the official Gazette, and shall come into force on such publication.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the words “Government”, “Bangladesh”, and “taka” or “Tk” were substituted for the words “Provincial Government”, “East Pakistan” and “rupees” or “Rs” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 Clause (f) was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 Clause (g) was omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 Clause (a) was omitted by section 2 of the Film Development Corporation (Amendment) Act, 1967 (East Pakistan Act No. XIV of 1967)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word “Dhaka” was substituted for the word “Dacca” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The words “Sonali Bank” were substituted for the words “National Bank of Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8 Sub-section (3) was substituted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9 The words, comma, figures and brackets “Companies Act, 1994 (Act 18 of 1994)” were substituted for the words, comma, figures and brackets “Companies Act, 1913 (VII of 1913)” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10 The words “and the Government of Pakistan” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">11 The word “Bangladesh” was substituted for the word “Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">12 The words, figures, comma and brackets “section 212 of the Companies Act, 1994 (Act 18 of 1994)” were substituted for the words, figures, comma and brackets “section 144 of the Companies Act, 1913 (VII of 1913)” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">13 The word “Parliament” was substituted for the words “the Provincial Legislature” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">14 The words, comma, figures and brackets “Income-tax Ordinance, 1984 (XXXVI of 1984)” were substituted for the words, comma, figures and brackets “Income-tax Act, 1922 (XI of 1922)” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
277	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE FINANCE ACT, 1957 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE FINANCE ACT, 1957 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(EAST PAKISTAN ACT NO. X OF 1957).[25th April, 1957]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 An Act to raise funds for augmentation of the revenues 2[ * * *] and for continuance in force of certain taxes for the purpose of meeting expenditure on rehabilitation of refugees.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to raise funds for augmentation of the revenues 3[ * * *] and to continue in force certain taxes for the purpose of meeting expenditure on rehabilitation of refugees as hereinafter provided;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It is, therefore, enacted as follows:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Act may be called the 4[ * * *] Finance Act, 1957.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It shall be deemed to have come into force from the 1st day of April, 1957.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Levy and collection of tax on advertisement through daily newspapers</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5[ 2. (1) There shall be levied and collected a tax on advertisement through daily newspapers excluding tender and employment notices, at the rate of ten per centum of the amount charged on such advertisement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The tax shall be collected and paid to the Government by the authority or management of the newspapers concerned.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The National Board of Revenue may make rules regulating the procedure for collection and payment of the tax and any other matter incidental to its levy.]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Levy and realisation of tax from owners, etc, of shops is certain areas</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) There shall be levied and collected from the owner or management of any shop situated in any Municipal or Cantonment Area or in such other area or areas as may be notified in the official Gazette a tax of Tk. 3 per annum.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Explanation.- ‘Shop' means any premises not being premises intended to be in the nature of a temporary structure, where the trade or business of selling goods by retail or wholesale is carried on by the owner or occupier, or where services are rendered by the owner or occupier to the customers, and includes offices, show-rooms, store-rooms, godowns or ware-houses, wherever situated, used in connection with the said trade or business.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government may make rules regulating the procedure for collection and payment of the tax and any other matter incidental to its levy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Amendment of Bengal Agricultural Income-Tax Act, 1944</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. [Amendment of Bengal Agricultural Income-Tax Act, 1944.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Registration of hotels, restaurants, eating houses and lodging houses</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) Every owner or management of a hotel, restaurant, eating house or lodging-house shall apply for registration to such officer, in such manner and within such time as may be prescribed by the Government by rules on payment of registration fee at the scales specified below:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. [Imposition of tax on jute.- Omitted by section 2 of the Finance (Amendment) Act, 1975 (Act No. XXXI of 1975).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. [Amendment of the Bengal Motor Vehicles Tax Act, 1932 and the Assam Motor Vehicles Taxation Act, 1936.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">8. [Omitted by section 7 (4) of the East Pakistan Ordinance No. LXV of 1958 which was also repealed by section 8 of the East Pakistan Act XII of 1958. ]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. [Payment of tax by legal and Income-tax practitioners.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">10. [Payment of tax by Clearing Agents and Contractors.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">11. [Toll on vessels plying in inland waters.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">12. [Toll on fares and freights on traffic by inland vessels.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13. [Toll on freights on goods carried by road.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">[]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">14. [Amendment of Art. 53 of Schedule I of Act II of 1899.- Omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Penalty</p><p style="text-align: justify;">15. If the person on whom the tax is levied or who is responsible for the collection and payment of any tax or toll under this Act fails to pay the tax or toll as provided in this Act and the rules made thereunder, he shall be liable to a penalty not exceeding the amount of the tax or toll payable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Public demand</p><p style="text-align: justify;">16. Any tax, toll or fee leviable under the provision of this Act or any penalty imposed thereunder shall be deemed to be public demand within the meaning of the 6[ * * *] Public Demands Recovery Act, 1913.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the words “Government” and “Tk.” were substituted for the words “Provincial Government” and “Rs.” Respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “of the Province” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The words “of the Province” were omitted by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 Section 2 was substituted by section 4 of the ???? ???, ???? (???? ???? ?? ?? ???)?</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The word “Bengal” was omitted by section 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
278	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE FINANCE (THIRD) ORDINANCE, 1958 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>THE FINANCE (THIRD) ORDINANCE, 1958 </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. LXXXII OF 1958).[26th December, 1958]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Ordinance to raise funds for the augmentation of the revenues of the Province and for that purpose to levy certain taxes.             1</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to raise funds for augmentation of the revenues of the Province and for that purpose to levy certain taxes as hereinafter provided;</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Presidential Proclamation of the 7th day of October, 1958 and in exercise of the powers enabling him in that behalf, the Governor is pleased to make and promulgate the following Ordinance, namely:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title and extent </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the 2[ * * *] Finance (Third) Ordinance, 1958.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of 3[ Bangladesh].</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Levy of development and relief tax</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. (1) There shall be levied and collected by the Government a development and relief tax from every tenant at the rate of four annas on each taka of rent payable by him in respect of the land comprised in his tenancy with effect from the 1st day of Baishakh, 1365 :</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that when such land is held free of rent, such development and relief tax shall be levied and collected at the rate of four annas on each taka of rent that would be assessable on such land on the principles laid down in section 26 of the 4[ * * *] State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The development and relief tax levied under sub-section (1) shall be realised in the manner in which rent is realised by the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3[Omitted]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. [Levy of additional stamp duty and manner of realization.- Omitted by section 10 of the Finance Act, 1980 (Act No. XXIII of 1980).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4[Repealed]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. [Repeal of section 2 of E.P. Act XII of 1958.- Repealed by section 3 and the Third Schedule of the Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1966 (East Pakistan Ordinance No. XIII of 1966).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Act, the words “Government” and “taka” were substituted for the words “Provincial Government” and “rupee” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The word “ Bangladesh” was substituted for the words “East Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “East Bengal” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Bangladesh Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Source : Ministry of Law, Justice and Parliamentary Affairs</p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p><p style="text-align: justify;"></p> </div></div>
279	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">THE FOREST INDUSTRIES DEVELOPMENT CORPORATION ORDINANCE, 1959 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p align="center"><strong>THE FOREST INDUSTRIES DEVELOPMENT CORPORATION ORDINANCE, 1959</strong></p><p align="center">(EAST PAKISTAN ORDINANCE NO. LXVII OF 1959)</p><p align="right">[3rd October, 1959]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">An Ordinance to establish a Corporation for the purpose of promoting the development of Forest Industries in Bangladesh.            1</p><p style="text-align: justify;">WHEREAS it is expedient to establish a Corporation for the purpose of promoting the development of Forest Industries and industries based on forest products and water resources in the Forest areas in Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">NOW, THEREFORE, in pursuance of the Presidential Proclamation of the seventh day of October, 1958, the Governor is pleased in exercise of all powers enabling him in that behalf, to make and promulgate the following Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Short title, extent and commencement </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">1. (1) This Ordinance may be called the 2[ * * *] Forest Industries Development Corporation Ordinance, 1959.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) It extends to the whole of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) It shall come into force on such date as the Government may, by notification in the official Gazette, appoint.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Interpretation </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">2. In this Ordinance, unless there is anything repugnant in the subject or context,-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a)        “Board” means the Board of Directors of the Corporation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b)        “Corporation” means Bangladesh Forest Industries Development Corporation established under this Ordinance;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c)        “Prescribed” means prescribed by rules or regulations under this Ordinance; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d)        “Schedule” means schedule appended to this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Establishment and incorporation</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">3. (1) As soon as may be after the commencement of this Ordinance, the Government shall establish a Corporation to be called “The Bangladesh Forest Industries Development Corporation”.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Corporation shall be a body corporate having perpetual succession and a common seal with power, subject to the provisions of this Ordinance, to acquire, hold and dispose of property both movable and immovable and shall by the said name sue and be sued.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Share Capital</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">4. (1) The authorised share capital of the Corporation shall be one crore of taka divided into ten thousand fully paid-up shares of one thousand taka each, of which two thousand five hundred shares shall be issued in the first instance and the remaining shares may be issued from time to time by the Corporation with the previous sanction of the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Government shall be a share holder of the Corporation and shall subscribe to and hold not less than fifty-one per centum of the shares issued by the Corporation at any time, the remaining shares being open for public subscription.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Nothing in sub-section (1) shall prevent the Corporation from increasing the authorised share capital as it may think fit with the previous sanction of the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Management</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">5. (1) The general direction and administration of the Corporation and its affairs shall vest in a Board, which may exercise all powers and do all acts and things which may be exercised or done by the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Board in discharging its functions shall act on commercial considerations and shall be guided on questions of policy involving the national interest (including commercial and industrial interest) by such directions as the Government, which shall be the sole judge whether the national interest is involved, may give it from time to time.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) If the Board fails to carry out any direction as aforesaid, the Government may remove the Directors including the Chairman, and notwithstanding anything contained in section 6, appoint persons in their place to be Directors temporarily until a fresh Board of Directors are appointed in accordance with the provision of that section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Appointment and terms of office of Directors</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">6. (1) The Board shall consist of not more than five Directors including Chairman to be appointed by the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Each Director shall:-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) be a wholetime officer of the Corporation;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) perform such duties as the Board may by regulations assign to him;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) divest himself of any directorship or other interest held by him in any Corporation, company or concern other than companies sponsored by the Corporation under sub-section (2) of section 14 before assuming office as Director;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) hold office for a term of three years unless sooner removed or transferred by the Government and may be appointed thereafter for a further term or terms of such duration as the Government may in appointing him thereafter, determine; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(e) receive such salary and allowances as the Government may determine:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that the Government may in exceptional circumstances where it considers necessary to do so in the public interest, exempt by a special order any person who has been appointed or is about to be appointed a Director from the operation of clauses (a) and (c) of this sub-section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Chairman</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">7. (1) The Government shall appoint one of the Directors to be the Chairman of the Board;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) Subject to his continuing to hold office as a Director, the Chairman shall hold office as Chairman for a term of three years and subject as aforesaid shall remain in office as Chairman thereafter until his successor in that office is appointed and be eligible to hold that office for a further like term or terms.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Disqualification of Directors</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">8.         (1) No person shall be or shall continue to be a Director who-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) is or at any time has been convicted of an offence involving moral turpitude; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) is or at any time has been adjudicated insolvent; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) is found to be lunatic or of unsound mind; or</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(d) is a minor.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) No Director shall continue in office after absenting himself from three consecutive meetings of the Board without the leave of absence from the Chairman, or, in the case of the Chairman, from the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) A Government servant serving as Chairman or a Director shall automatically cease to be the Chairman or a Director of the Corporation, as the case may be, on his transfer from the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Appointment of officers, etc</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">9. The Corporation may appoint such officers, advisers and employees as it considers necessary for the efficient performance of its functions on such terms and conditions as may be prescribed by rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Meeting of the Board</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">10.       (1) The meeting of the Board shall be held at such time and such places as may be prescribed by rules:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that until rules are made in this behalf such meetings shall be convened by the Chairman of the Board.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) To constitute a quorum at a meeting of the Board, not less than two Directors shall be present.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) Each Director including the Chairman shall have one vote, and in the event of an equality of votes the Chairman shall have a second or casting vote.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) If for any reason the Chairman is unable to be present at a meeting, the Director so authorised by him in writing shall preside at the meeting, and in default of such authorisation, the Directors shall elect from among themselves a Chairman to preside at that meeting.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Head Office</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">11.       The Corporation shall establish its head office in Dhaka.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Deposit Account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">12.       The Corporation may open a deposit account with the 3[ Bangladesh Bank] or with any agency of the 4[ Bangladesh Bank] other than a Government Treasury or with the prior approval of the Government, with any other Scheduled Bank.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Investment Funds</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">13.       The Corporation may invest its funds in such securities of the 5[ Government] or in such other manners as may be prescribed by rules.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Business which the Corporation shall transact</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">14.       (1) The Corporation shall submit, for the approval of the Government, schemes for the establishment of the industries specified in the Schedule to this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) The Corporation shall, as soon as may be, proceed to give effect to any scheme so approved by sponsoring public companies (hereinafter referred to in this section as ‘The aforesaid companies') incorporated under the 6[ Companies Act, 1994 (Act No. 18 of 1994)], and independent of each other and having as their object manufacturing undertakings in the industry concerned:</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that before sponsoring any such company the Corporation shall obtain the approval of the Government to the Company's capital structure.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(3) The Corporation shall unless otherwise directed by the Government, act as Managing Agents for the aforesaid companies, and may, with the prior concurrence of the Government, relinquish the managing agency in favour of any company.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(4) Nothing in 7[ section 160 of the Companies Act, 1994 (Act No. 18 of 1994)], shall apply to the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(5) The Corporation shall be represented in the Board of Directors of the aforesaid Companies.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(6) The Corporation may issue the capital required by the aforesaid companies for public subscription and if any portion thereof remains unsubscribed for a period of four months from the date of issue it shall be subscribed by the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(7) The Corporation may underwrite the whole or any portion of the share capital so issued.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(8) The Corporation may when it deems fit sell or transfer the shares subscribed by it under sub-section (6) :</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provided that no such sale or transfer shall take place at a rate below the market quotation and below the per value of such shares without the previous sanction of the Government.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(9) The Corporation may, with the previous sanction of the Government and on such terms and conditions as may be approved by the Government, borrow in foreign currency from any International Bank or otherwise moneys required for development of industries specified in the schedule to this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Audit</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">15.       The Government shall appoint auditors who shall be persons holding a certificate under 8[ section 212 of the Companies Act, 1994 (Act No. 18 of 1994)] on such remuneration as it may fix and such remuneration shall be paid by the Corporation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Account</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">16.       An audited statement of accounts shall be furnished to the Government by the Corporation as soon as possible after the end of every financial year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Annual Report</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">17. The Corporation shall, as soon as possible after the end of every financial year, submit an annual report to the Government on the conduct of its affairs for that year, and on its proposals for the next ensuing financial year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of Government to make rules</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">18.       The Government may make rules not inconsistent with this Ordinance for the purpose of giving effect to the provision of this Ordinance and where the rules made under this section are inconsistent with the regulations made under the next succeeding section, the rules shall prevail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power of Board to make Regulations</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">19.       (1) The Board may, with the previous approval of the Government, make regulations not inconsistent with this Ordinance or rules made thereunder to provide for all matters for which provision is necessary or expedient for the purpose of giving effect to the provisions of this Ordinance.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(2) In particular and without prejudice to the generality of the foregoing powers, such regulations may provide for-</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(a) the procedure of meeting of the Board;</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(b) the investment of the Corporation's funds; and</p><p style="text-align: justify;">(c) the sale or transfer of shares under sub-section (8) of section 14.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Power to amend schedule</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">20.       The Government may, from time to time, by notification in the official Gazette amend the schedule to this Ordinance so as to include therein or exclude therefrom any industry or vary the description of any industry included therein.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b>Repeal of East Pakistan Ordinance LXIII of 1958</b></p><p style="text-align: justify;">21.       [Repeal of East Pakistan Ordinance LXIII of 1958.- Repealed by section 2 and the First Schedule of the East Pakistan Repealing and Amending Ordinance, 1966 (East Pakistan Ordinance No. XIII of 1966).]</p><p style="text-align: justify;">_____________________________________________________</p><p style="text-align: justify;">1 Throughout this Ordinance, the words “Bangladesh”, “Government” and “taka” were substituted for the words “East Pakistan”, “Provincial Government” and “rupees” respectively by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">2 The words “East Pakistan” were omitted by Article 6 of the Bangladesh (Adaptation of Existing Laws) Order, 1972 (President's Order No. 48 of 1972)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">3 The words “Bangladesh Bank” were substituted for the words “State Bank of Pakistan” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">4 The words “Bangladesh Bank” were substituted for the words “State Bank” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">5 The word “Government” was substituted for the words “Provincial or the Central Government” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">6 The words, comma, figures and brackets “Companies Act, 1994 (Act No. 18 of 1994)” were substituted for the words, comma, figures and brackets “Companies Act, 1913 (VII of 1913)” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision And Declaration) Act, 1973 (Act No. VIII of 1973)</p><p style="text-align: justify;">7 The words, figures, comma and brackets “section 160 of the Companies Act, 1994 (Act No. 18 of 1994) ” were substituted for the words, figures, comma and brackets “section 87A of the Companies Act, 1913 (VII of 1913) ” by section 3 and the Second Schedule of the Bangladesh Laws (Revision
